Found this treasure today by mere coincidence.. What an amazing place! Super clean and neat.
The raspados are so authentic! Just like what we used to have on our vacations in Guadalajara growing up. Everything is natural and made from scratch..none of that artificial gooey stuff others use. The flavors are prepared to perfection..awesome variety of flavors. Had the privilege  of meeting the owner, Oscar. Super nice, down to earth person that wants and makes sure his customers are happy and satisfied with the service they receive. I can't wait for him to open a place in South County. We definitely need something like this there. They would undoubtedly be a hit. Until then , I'll be driving to Santa Ana to satisfy my craving of authentic raspados and to try all the other neat treats and yummy stuff they sell.
Today we tried the walnut and coconut  (you can mix flavors too) as well as the pineapple.
OUTSTANDING!!!!! Can't wait til next time to try something new. Thanks Oscar for bringing this to the O.C.!!!</review>

Richard, Steven, and Victor are the nicest young men around. I was very emotional about letting go of my piano and when Richard noticed it he said some very nice things to help me. They were careful with it and made me feel like they were the boys next door helping me move a family piece to a new home. It was not an easy piece to move; an old player piano easily three times the weight of a regular upright. They moved it as gracefully as possible and didn't give it the slightest bump or nick.

I called the "boss" right away and told him about the men and how careful, compassionate and caring they were. He was just as kind. He took great pride in knowing his company was represented well. He made it a point to say that it's one thing to hire strong guys to lift "stuff" and it's entirely another thing to hire good men to haul away your items with as much care as possible - both for the item and for the customer.

In today's corporate world, it's not always easy to find a company with compassionate employees who are able to assess how someone is feeling and make them a little more comfortable. These three did just that. And, clearly, the owner is mindful of this.

I will definitely call these gentlemen again when we do some spring cleaning and I will absolutely recommend them to everyone I know.

Oh! And the price was well within reason. It was, in fact, the lowest quote I got. But all in all, what I valued most was how kind this group of young men were.

Thank you, Justin, for hiring great guys.
Thank you, Richard, Steven, and Victor, for making this morning a little easier for me. I appreciate you.< /Review>

We haven't patronized C'Era Una Volta for over a decade, for good reason. We have high expectations with Italian food and unfortunately they did not improve with time.    The best part of the meal was probably the bread, served with a warm, mustardy aioli that was both smooth and pungent, creamy but not spicy.  The beet salad was so uninspiring, we could have done better putting a few pkgs from Trader Joes in a bowl and assembling something ourselves. Our daughter's kids' sausage pizza was served with mushrooms (wasn't mentioned on the menu), husband's melanzane Parmigiana was decent, but my Tagliolini alla Senese was a let-down. There was a giant clump of uncooked, unseparated noodles, and the sauce was supposed to be a chianti beef sauce but all I could get was tons of herbaceousness from a heavy hand (I forgot if it was thyme or rosemary, it wasn't pleasant). The service was very lackluster (took a while to take our order, arms reaching across the table instead of going around to serve/clear, no one checked on us after our main courses were delivered). I truly wish they would improve because I would throw my money at a good Italian reataurant without a second thought (yes, we've been to Italy, from Roma up to Venezia) but it isn't this place.< /Text>

I came in at lunchtime, and they have a limited menu, if you come in early, like I did. I had the porcini panini, and it was delicious. It also came with a side salad that had a mustard-like dressing. I also had the pompelmo (grapefruit) San Pellegrino soda, but their other flavors are also available. I plan on going back for dinner, which starts at 4pm local time. My server was very friendly, which is always appreciated. I was also given the option to either sit inside or on the patio, and since it's a nice day, I sat outside. The parking is always challenging, but that is through no fault of the establishment. I recommend C'Era Una Volta.< /text>

<rating>5< /rating><Review>I don't offer 5 stars much if at all, but here we are.
Wait staff, preparation, ambiance were all spot on. Our waiter was attentive and caring. I was a bit overwhelmed by the wine list and asked for help with a huge selection of Italian and other European reds. So our waiter called in the de facto wine steward. That person asked a couple of simple questions, made her recommendation and nailed it.
Gluten free options for my dining partner, the Tortelloni Ai Porcini for me.
As the place filled up we never felt rushed. Our waiter constantly reminded us through dinner, wine, dessert and coffee to "take our time."
